<analysis>**original_problem_statement:**
The user initially requested to implement visual rendering (SVG) for all geometric figures generated by the backend. Throughout the session, the user also identified and requested fixes for several critical bugs:
1.  **SVG Rendering Quality:** The initial SVGs for Circles and Rectangles were illegible (too small, overlapping text).
2.  **Missing SVGs:** An audit revealed that some geometric generators (, ) were not producing the necessary data to render an SVG.
3.  **Missing :** Exercises were sometimes appearing in the frontend with no text statement ().
4.  **Thales Figure Incoherence:** The  and  for Thales' theorem exercises used different, hardcoded point names that did not match the generated SVG figure, making the exercises incorrect and unusable.
5.  **Application Unavailability:** A recurring environment issue caused the backend to fail on startup, preventing the user from testing the application.

**PRODUCT REQUIREMENTS:**
- All geometric exercises (Pythagoras, Trigonometry, Thales, Circles, Rectangles, etc.) must be rendered as clean, legible SVG figures.
- The  (statement) and  text must be 100% consistent with the data and points shown in the SVG figure.
- The application must be stable and consistently available for testing after a restart.
- The system must have robust fallbacks to prevent inconsistent or empty data from reaching the user.
- Automated tests must be in place to validate data coherence and SVG generation.

**User's preferred language**: French

**what currently exists?**
The application now successfully generates and renders SVG figures for all relevant geometric exercises. The backend logic for rendering has been significantly improved for readability, especially for circles and rectangles. A series of critical bugs related to data consistency have been fixed. Specifically, the Thales generator is now fully coherent, with both the  and  dynamically using the correct points from the figure. The fallback mechanisms have been hardened to ensure an  is always generated. Several new automated test suites have been created to prevent regressions for SVG generation and data coherence. However, the application environment is unstable and requires manual intervention to start the backend after every container restart.

Usage: apt-get [options] command
       apt-get [options] install|remove pkg1 [pkg2 ...]
       apt-get [options] source pkg1 [pkg2 ...]

apt-get is a command line interface for retrieval of packages
and information about them from authenticated sources and
for installation, upgrade and removal of packages together
with their dependencies.

Most used commands:
  update - Retrieve new lists of packages
  upgrade - Perform an upgrade
  install - Install new packages (pkg is libc6 not libc6.deb)
  reinstall - Reinstall packages (pkg is libc6 not libc6.deb)
  remove - Remove packages
  purge - Remove packages and config files
  autoremove - Remove automatically all unused packages
  dist-upgrade - Distribution upgrade, see apt-get(8)
  dselect-upgrade - Follow dselect selections
  build-dep - Configure build-dependencies for source packages
  satisfy - Satisfy dependency strings
  clean - Erase downloaded archive files
  autoclean - Erase old downloaded archive files
  check - Verify that there are no broken dependencies
  source - Download source archives
  download - Download the binary package into the current directory
  changelog - Download and display the changelog for the given package

See apt-get(8) for more information about the available commands.
Configuration options and syntax is detailed in apt.conf(5).
Information about how to configure sources can be found in sources.list(5).
Package and version choices can be expressed via apt_preferences(5).
Security details are available in apt-secure(8).

**Code Architecture**


**Key Technical Concepts**
- **Hybrid Architecture**: Python for deterministic logic, AI for text generation.
- **Dynamic SVG Rendering**: Generating SVG strings on the fly from structured geometric data.
- **Robust Fallbacks**: A multi-layered fallback system ensuring that if an AI or specific template fails, a generic but valid response is still generated.
- **Data Coherence Validation**: Programmatically validating AI output against a source of truth (the math spec) before accepting it.
- **Environment Dependency Management**: The critical (and currently failing) need to manage system-level libraries () within the containerized environment.
